Webinar! NOAA/NSTA Science Update:*=C2=A0*Observing Hurricanes with Ocean=
 Drones

saildrone [ https://www.pmel.noaa.gov/saildrone-hurricane/?utm_medium=3De=
mail&utm_source=3DGovDelivery ]=20

Dr. Greg Foltz, an oceanographer at NOAA's Atlantic Oceanographic and Met=
eorological Laboratory in Miami is the the co-lead of=C2=A0NOAA's Saildro=
ne Hurricane Observations [ https://www.pmel.noaa.gov/saildrone-hurricane=
/?utm_medium=3Demail&utm_source=3DGovDelivery ], which aims to improve ou=
r understanding of hurricanes and aid forecasts. During this presentation=
, he will describe a new NOAA project to direct surface ocean drones ("sa=
ildrones") into hurricanes in the Atlantic Ocean and discuss what saildro=
nes are, how they work and can survive a hurricane, what kind of data (an=
d videos!) we get from them, and how the data is being used to aid foreca=
sters and improve our understanding of hurricanes. Join us!

Find more information and register for the webinar. [ https://my.nsta.org=
/event/science-update-observing-hurricanes-with-ocean-drones-june-8-2023?=
utm_medium=3Demail&utm_source=3DGovDelivery ]

Celebrate National Ocean Month with NOS!

ocean month [ https://oceanservice.noaa.gov/ocean/30days/?utm_medium=3Dem=
ail&utm_source=3DGovDelivery ]=20

NOAA=C2=A0is dedicated to addressing the evolving economic, environmental=
, and social pressures on our oceans. As such, this month provides us wit=
h a unique opportunity to raise awareness about the ocean and highlight o=
ur efforts in safeguarding it. Join us all June as we celebrate National =
Ocean Month. We will be sharing videos, imagery, and trivia about our oce=
an and coasts with a different theme each week:


  * June 1-3: Corals (past)=20
  * =C2=A0June 4-10: New Blue Economy=20
  * June 11-17: The Ocean is for Everyone=20
  * June 18-24: Conserve, Restore, and Connect to Coastal and Marine Ecos=
ystems=20
  * June 25-20: Coastal Resilience=20

You can participate in the festivities by visiting the NOS National Ocean=
 Month webpage [ https://oceanservice.noaa.gov/ocean/30days/?utm_medium=3D=
email&utm_source=3DGovDelivery ] and following us on Facebook [ https://w=
ww.facebook.com/usoceangov/?utm_medium=3Demail&utm_source=3DGovDelivery ]=
, Twitter [ https://twitter.com/noaaocean?utm_medium=3Demail&utm_source=3D=

nstagram.com/noaaocean/?utm_medium=3Demail&utm_source=3DGovDelivery ] to =

*NOAA Teachers on the Estuary Workshops*

When: June 13 to August 11, and other times during the school year

NOAA=E2=80=99s National Estuarine Research Reserve System [ https://coast=
.noaa.gov/estuaries/?utm_medium=3Demail&utm_source=3DGovDelivery ] (NERRS=
) holds Teachers on the Estuary (TOTE) workshops [ https://coast.noaa.gov=
/estuaries/teachers-on-the-estuary/calendar.html?utm_medium=3Demail&utm_s=
ource=3DGovDelivery ]=C2=A0research and field-based training programs for=
 K=E2=80=9312 teachers held at research reserve sites across the country.=
 TOTE workshops offer a minimum of 15 contact hours, giving teachers the =
opportunity to


  * Explore coastal habitats and conduct field investigations;=20
  * Interact with local scientists and experienced coastal educators;=20
  * Integrate local and national monitoring data into the classroom; and=20=

  * Learn hands-on field activities highlighting various=C2=A0Estuary Edu=
cation Resources [ https://coast.noaa.gov/estuaries/curriculum/?utm_mediu=
m=3Demail&utm_source=3DGovDelivery ].=20

With TOTE, teachers and students interact with scientists, find informati=
on about local environmental issues, and participate in field trips and c=
ommunity conservation projects. Some workshops are free of charge and/or =
offer stipends upon completion. Advance registration is required.

14 June 2023 | 1:00 - 2:00 pm ET

*Juvenile snow crab habitat and response to warming in the Chukchi Sea* [=
 https://global.gotomeeting.com/join/891851101?utm_medium=3Demail&utm_sou=
rce=3DGovDelivery ]

Juvenile snow crab habitat in the Chukchi Sea was studied during a period=
 of ocean warming. During a cold year early in study, most juvenile crab =
of all sizes inhabited cold (<2C) areas. In later years, the smallest siz=
e classes were restricted to cold areas, or were effectively absent, and =
larger juveniles were present in warmer areas. Juvenile snow crab could b=
e impacted by the recent reduction in habitat with cold summer bottom tem=
perature in the Chukchi Sea (and Bering Sea).

omeone wondering how to get started doing collaborative science, this web=

29 June 2023 | 9:30 - 10:30 am ET

*U.S. Eastern Region Climate Services: Heat Season Preparedness and City =
Pilots* [ https://register.gotowebinar.com/rt/8640944652335396109?utm_med=
ium=3Demail&utm_source=3DGovDelivery ]

29 June 2023 | 12:00 - 1:00 pm ET

*Autonomous High-Resolution Ocean Floor Mapping* [ https://register.gotow=
ebinar.com/register/2211659274259940958?utm_medium=3Demail&utm_source=3DG=
ovDelivery ]

Mapping of the ocean floor is a major challenge because no existing techn=
ology offers both high-resolution and fast coverage rate. Meter-scale res=
olution, necessary for search and resource exploration, are obtained by s=
ending sensors deep into the ocean =E2=80=93 a slow and difficult approac=
h to mapping large areas. Low-frequency sonar can propagate across long d=
istances underwater providing fast coverage, but there are major limits t=
o resolution. A novel future approach could deploy a small fleet of USVs =
to create an array ten to a hundred times larger than existing, fixed hul=
l-mounted arrays. This larger array produces a narrower beam enabling hig=
her resolution maps at deeper depths. To demonstrate this a team conducte=
d a series of deployments in Cape Cod Bay.

2023 Jearld Lecture - Geosciencing While Black

" 20 Years of Unsettling Racial Discrimination and the White Gaze in Eart=
h Sciences Research and Workforce Preparation"

Wednesday, June 28, 2023 | 1:00 pm ET

Racism in Geo [ https://whoi-edu.zoom.us/webinar/register/WN_hrGimHdVRpC5=
-dN5gA8ffw?utm_medium=3Demail&utm_source=3DGovDelivery#/registration ]=20=


The Geoscience community is a microcosm of the larger STEM community as w=
ell as US society. Calls to eradicate systemic racism in U.S. institution=
s have both been amplified and received greater attention over the past f=
ew decades. Systemic racism is a multidimensional challenge that often fr=
ames the day-to-day experiences of both racialized scientists and their =E2=
=80=9Cseemingly=E2=80=9C unracialized counterparts. This talk will discus=
s six forms of erasure that undergird racial discrimination in science an=
d how they manifest, then highlight a number of programs and countermeasu=
res to the numerous systemic factors entrenching racism in STEM. Presente=
d by Dr. Vernon Morris, Foundation Professor and Associate Dean of Knowle=
dge Enterprise and Strategic Outcomes in the New College of Interdiscipli=
nary Arts and Sciences at Arizona State University. Register now. [ https=
://whoi-edu.zoom.us/webinar/register/WN_hrGimHdVRpC5-dN5gA8ffw?utm_medium=
=3Demail&utm_source=3DGovDelivery#/registration ]

*NOAA Ship "Okeanos Explorer" *

*Seascape Alaska 2023,=C2=A0* [ https://oceanexplorer.noaa.gov/okeanos/ex=
plorations/seascape-alaska/welcome.html?utm_medium=3Demail&utm_source=3DG=
ovDelivery ]May 5 - October 14, 2023

NOAA and its partners will conduct six expeditions mapping the seafloor a=
nd using remotely operated vehicles (ROVs) to collect information to clos=
e gaps in our understanding of one of the least explored but incredibly e=
conomically and culturally important areas in the United States: Alaska. =
This expedition will focus on deepwater areas in the Gulf of Alaska, Aleu=
tian Islands, and the Aleutian Trench. ROV dives from 250 to 6,000 meters=
 deep are anticipated from June 29 - July 24=C2=A0 and August 24 - Septem=
ber 15 and will explore seafloor subduction zones, deep-sea coral and spo=
nge habitats, seamounts, mud volcanoes, hydrothermal vents, marine minera=
ls, underwater cultural heritage sites, and the water column.

"Seascape Alaska" [ https://storymaps.arcgis.com/stories/094abb14281e4b24=
89146a3f3e030961?utm_medium=3Demail&utm_source=3DGovDelivery ]" is a mult=
iyear, multipartner cooperative research campaign to create accessible, h=
igh-quality modern seabed data for Alaskan waters to support U.S. researc=
h, resource management, sustainable economic growth, and the health and s=
ecurity of Americans."

*R/V "Falkor (too)", Schmidt Ocean Institute*

*Octopus Odyssey* [ https://schmidtocean.org/cruise/octopus-odyssey/?utm_=
medium=3Demail&utm_source=3DGovDelivery ]*, Costa Rica,=C2=A0*June 2023

This expedition will investigate the biodiversity of unprotected seamount=
s in an under-explored region in Costa Rica. The primary target is the Do=
rado Outcrop, where a =E2=80=9Cgarden=E2=80=9D of female octopuses was fi=
rst discovered in 2013 brooding their eggs along low-temperature vents, a=
 phenomenon scientists had never seen before. The goal for this expeditio=
n is to better understand the hydrogeology, microbiology, ecology, and ge=
ochemistry that may facilitate this fascinating behavior.

*To stay up to date on where these three ships are and tune in via the De=
ep Ocean Education Project website **Vessels page.* [ https://deepoceaned=
ucation.org/vessels/?utm_medium=3Demail&utm_source=3DGovDelivery ]

*Tracking Water Using NASA Satellite Data*

In this activity for grades 4=E2=80=938, students use real NASA satellite=
 data to track water mass changes, learn how to read a heat map, and disc=
uss the local and global implications of their findings. The activity inc=
ludes embedded videos describing the science behind NASA=E2=80=99s GRACE =
(Gravity Research And Climate Experiment). In addition to the lesson=E2=80=
=99s overview, background information, and procedures, the plan includes =
classroom management tips, assessments, and suggested extensions. Check i=
t out! [ https://www.jpl.nasa.gov/edu/teach/activity/tracking-water-using=
-nasa-satellite-data?utm_medium=3Demail&utm_source=3DGovDelivery ]

Exploring by the Seat of Your Pants [ https://www.exploringbytheseat.com/=
?utm_medium=3Demail&utm_source=3DGovDelivery ] (EBTSOYP) works to inspire=
 the next generation of scientists and explorers by hosting virtual guest=
 speakers and field trips most appropriate for middle and high school cla=
ssrooms. EBTSOYP Daily Dives present classrooms with a short (5- to 7-min=
ute) videos and a brief (5-minute) thought-provoking activity highlightin=
g a current science research breakthrough, conservation story, expedition=
, or other science event each day. Recent topics have addressed zombie-an=
t fungi, Arctic cyclones, bubble blowing echidnas, hunting meteorites, an=
d the submersible Alvin. The Daily Dives playlist can be viewed on the=C2=
=A0EBTSOYP YouTube channel [ https://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=3DPLwK=
FsJZmdxpHfV5D7vYlo8o_RdmFxeo2d&utm_medium=3Demail&utm_source=3DGovDeliver=
y ]. Teachers can access the accompanying student activity and a transcri=
pt for the video in the video=E2=80=99s YouTube description.=C2=A0

Breathe In, Breathe Out

Trace the flow of energy from the Sun to the cells in organisms using the=
 new Click & Learn "Energy Flow through Ecosystems" [ https://www.biointe=
ractive.org/classroom-resources/energy-flow-through-ecosystems?utm_medium=
=3Demail&utm_source=3DGovDelivery ], which includes embedded questions an=
d calculations about the distribution of energy within ecosystems. Explor=
e patterns in the Keeling Curve with the new Click & Learn "The Breathing=
 Biosphere and Human Contribution" [ https://www.biointeractive.org/class=
room-resources/breathing-biosphere-and-human-contribution?utm_medium=3Dem=
ail&utm_source=3DGovDelivery ], which discusses natural and anthropogenic=
 processes that contribute to atmospheric carbon dioxide.

*Making Connections*

Models represent systems of interrelated ideas, events, or processes. The=
 "Model Builder" [ https://www.biointeractive.org/classroom-resources/mod=
el-builder?utm_medium=3Demail&utm_source=3DGovDelivery ] allows students =
to generate and refine a variety of models to show relationships and make=
 predictions about biological phenomena. Use a model from the collection =
developed by BioInteractive [ https://www.biointeractive.org/?utm_medium=3D=
email&utm_source=3DGovDelivery ], or have students generate their own mod=
els with provided graphics. The tool also includes an automated self-chec=
k feature for students and allows educators to score students=E2=80=99 mo=
dels automatically.

Grants=20

*Investing in Our Ocean Future:=C2=A0 STEM Education Grants to Broaden Ac=
cess to Ocean Sciences *

*Proposals Accepted: June 15 - August 15, 2023 *

The National Marine Sanctuary Foundation, in cooperation with NOAA Ocean =
Exploration, is excited to once again offer grants to educators and educa=
tion programs leading workforce development initiatives that advance dive=
rsity, equity, inclusion, and accessibility in ocean science and/or explo=
ration career pathways. The overarching goal is to support a future ocean=
 workforce that is more representative of US demographics by funding proj=
ects that minimize barriers to entry and retention of diverse youth from =
communities historically marginalized from ocean science and exploration =
industries. These grants are an investment in projects and partners that =
are leading science, education, technology, and engineering (STEM) educat=
ion programming for diverse youth in middle school, high school, undergra=
duate, and/or community college to learn about the ocean, develop or adva=
nce STEM skills, and increase awareness of ocean science careers.

Learn more about the grants and explore previously funded projects! [ htt=
ps://oceanexplorer.noaa.gov/edu/deia-grants/welcome.html?utm_medium=3Dema=
il&utm_source=3DGovDelivery ]__

      <p style=3D"margin-bottom: 1.0em; color: #232323; font: 13px/1.5 Aria=

mprove our understanding of hurricanes and aid forecasts. During this prese=
ntation, he will describe a new NOAA project to direct surface ocean drones=

<h1 style=3D"font-size: 20px; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; ma=
rgin: 0 0 5px; padding: 0;"><strong>NOAA Teachers on the Estuary Workshops<=
/strong></h1>

rgin: 3px 0 4px; padding: 0;">When: June 13 to August 11, and other times d=
uring the school year</h3>
<p style=3D"margin-bottom: 1.0em; color: #232323; font: 13px/1.5 Arial, Hel=

#1D5782;">NOAA=E2=80=99s National Estuarine Research Reserve System</a> (NE=
RRS) holds <a href=3D"https://lnks.gd/l/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiJ9.eyJidWxsZXRpbl=

045/br/204281882781-l" style=3D"color: #1D5782;">Teachers on the Estuary (T=

=80=9312 teachers held at research reserve sites across the country. TOTE w=
orkshops offer a minimum of 15 contact hours, giving teachers the opportuni=

<ul style=3D"font: 13px/1.5 Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;">
<li style=3D"color: #232323;">Explore coastal habitats and conduct field in=

into the classroom; and</li>
<li style=3D"color: #232323;">Learn hands-on field activities highlighting =
various&nbsp;<a href=3D"https://lnks.gd/l/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiJ9.eyJidWxsZXRp=

color: #1D5782;">Estuary Education Resources</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p style=3D"margin-bottom: 1.0em; color: #232323; font: 13px/1.5 Arial, Hel=
vetica, sans-serif;">With TOTE, teachers and students interact with scienti=

<h3 style=3D"text-align: center; font-size: 15px; font-family: Arial, Helve=
tica, sans-serif; margin: 3px 0 4px; padding: 0;" align=3D"center">14 June =
2023 | 1:00 - 2:00 pm ET</h3>
<p style=3D"text-align: center; margin-bottom: 1.0em; color: #232323; font:=
 13px/1.5 Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;" align=3D"center"><a href=3D"https:=
//lnks.gd/l/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiJ9.eyJidWxsZXRpbl9saW5rX2lkIjoxNDIsInVyaSI6Im=
JwMjpjbGljayIsInVybCI6Imh0dHBzOi8vZ2xvYmFsLmdvdG9tZWV0aW5nLmNvbS9qb2luLzg5M=
Tg1MTEwMT91dG1fbWVkaXVtPWVtYWlsJnV0bV9zb3VyY2U9R292RGVsaXZlcnkiLCJidWxsZXRp=
bl9pZCI6IjIwMjMwNjA2Ljc3ODEwMzIxIn0.apkYYwq1Ip_G_o09kWv14K3vQ-khfS9Rpfii9bT=
eOSM/s/3006607045/br/204281882781-l" style=3D"color: #1D5782;"><strong>Juve=
nile snow crab habitat and response to warming in the Chukchi Sea</strong><=
/a></p>
<p style=3D"text-align: left; margin-bottom: 1.0em; color: #232323; font: 1=
3px/1.5 Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;" align=3D"left">Juvenile snow crab ha=
bitat in the Chukchi Sea was studied during a period of ocean warming. Duri=
ng a cold year early in study, most juvenile crab of all sizes inhabited co=
ld (&lt;2C) areas. In later years, the smallest size classes were restricte=
d to cold areas, or were effectively absent, and larger juveniles were pres=
ent in warmer areas. Juvenile snow crab could be impacted by the recent red=
uction in habitat with cold summer bottom temperature in the Chukchi Sea (a=
nd Bering Sea).</p>

<p style=3D"text-align: center; margin-bottom: 1.0em; color: #232323; font:=
 13px/1.5 Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;" align=3D"center"><a href=3D"https:=

1D5782;"><strong>Career Pathways to Collaborative Science Success</strong><=
/a></p>
<p style=3D"text-align: left; margin-bottom: 1.0em; color: #232323; font: 1=
3px/1.5 Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;" align=3D"left">Curious about collabo=
rative science but unsure how to get started? Maybe you=E2=80=99re an early=
 career scientist and you=E2=80=99re worried that collaborative science goa=
ls won=E2=80=99t align with the rewards of the academic tenure-track system=
. Or maybe you=E2=80=99re a resource manager intrigued about the advantages=
 of a collaborative approach but you=E2=80=99re not sure how it could fit i=
nto your work. No matter your career track or level of experience, collabor=
ative science should be accessible and that there are countless entry point=
s and pathways to success. If you are someone wondering how to get started =
doing collaborative science, this webinar is for you.</p>

<p style=3D"text-align: center; margin-bottom: 1.0em; color: #232323; font:=

><strong>U.S. Eastern Region Climate Services: Heat Season Preparedness and=
 City Pilots</strong></a></p>

<h3 style=3D"text-align: center; font-size: 15px; font-family: Arial, Helve=
tica, sans-serif; margin: 3px 0 4px; padding: 0;" align=3D"center">29 June =
2023 | 12:00 - 1:00 pm ET</h3>
<p style=3D"text-align: center; margin-bottom: 1.0em; color: #232323; font:=
 13px/1.5 Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;" align=3D"center"><a href=3D"https:=
//lnks.gd/l/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiJ9.eyJidWxsZXRpbl9saW5rX2lkIjoxNDUsInVyaSI6Im=
JwMjpjbGljayIsInVybCI6Imh0dHBzOi8vcmVnaXN0ZXIuZ290b3dlYmluYXIuY29tL3JlZ2lzd=
GVyLzIyMTE2NTkyNzQyNTk5NDA5NTg_dXRtX21lZGl1bT1lbWFpbCZ1dG1fc291cmNlPUdvdkRl=
bGl2ZXJ5IiwiYnVsbGV0aW5faWQiOiIyMDIzMDYwNi43NzgxMDMyMSJ9.Xy5vMlJDhDSgEAftA7=
b4zaj8ajERDURyNvvczOPmnGw/s/3006607045/br/204281882781-l" style=3D"color: #=
1D5782;"><strong>Autonomous High-Resolution Ocean Floor Mapping</strong></a=
></p>
<p style=3D"text-align: left; margin-bottom: 1.0em; color: #232323; font: 1=
3px/1.5 Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;" align=3D"left">Mapping of the ocean =
floor is a major challenge because no existing technology offers both high-=
resolution and fast coverage rate. Meter-scale resolution, necessary for se=
arch and resource exploration, are obtained by sending sensors deep into th=
e ocean =E2=80=93 a slow and difficult approach to mapping large areas. Low=
-frequency sonar can propagate across long distances underwater providing f=
ast coverage, but there are major limits to resolution. A novel future appr=
oach could deploy a small fleet of USVs to create an array ten to a hundred=
 times larger than existing, fixed hull-mounted arrays. This larger array p=
roduces a narrower beam enabling higher resolution maps at deeper depths. T=
o demonstrate this a team conducted a series of deployments in Cape Cod Bay=
.</p>

arger STEM community as well as US society. Calls to eradicate systemic rac=

ntion over the past few decades. Systemic racism is a multidimensional chal=
lenge that often frames the day-to-day experiences of both racialized scien=
tists and their =E2=80=9Cseemingly=E2=80=9C unracialized counterparts. This=
 talk will discuss six forms of erasure that undergird racial discriminatio=
n in science and how they manifest, then highlight a number of programs and=
 countermeasures to the numerous systemic factors entrenching racism in STE=
M. Presented by Dr. Vernon Morris, Foundation Professor and Associate Dean =
of Knowledge Enterprise and Strategic Outcomes in the New College of Interd=
isciplinary Arts and Sciences at Arizona State University. <a href=3D"https=
://lnks.gd/l/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiJ9.eyJidWxsZXRpbl9saW5rX2lkIjoxNjcsInVyaSI6I=

<p style=3D"margin-bottom: 1.0em; color: #232323; font: 13px/1.5 Arial, Hel=
vetica, sans-serif;">NOAA and its partners will conduct six expeditions map=
ping the seafloor and using remotely operated vehicles (ROVs) to collect in=
formation to close gaps in our understanding of one of the least explored b=
ut incredibly economically and culturally important areas in the United Sta=
tes: Alaska. This expedition will focus on deepwater areas in the Gulf of A=
laska, Aleutian Islands, and the Aleutian Trench. ROV dives from 250 to 6,0=
00 meters deep are anticipated from June 29 - July 24&nbsp; and August 24 -=
 September 15 and will explore seafloor subduction zones, deep-sea coral an=
d sponge habitats, seamounts, mud volcanoes, hydrothermal vents, marine min=
erals, underwater cultural heritage sites, and the water column.</p>

to create accessible, high-quality modern seabed data for Alaskan waters to=

<p style=3D"margin-bottom: 1.0em; color: #232323; font: 13px/1.5 Arial, Hel=
vetica, sans-serif;"><a href=3D"https://lnks.gd/l/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiJ9.eyJi=

-l" style=3D"color: #1D5782;"><strong>Octopus Odyssey</strong></a><strong>,=
 Costa Rica,&nbsp;</strong>June 2023</p>
<p style=3D"margin-bottom: 1.0em; color: #232323; font: 13px/1.5 Arial, Hel=
vetica, sans-serif;">This expedition will investigate the biodiversity of u=
nprotected seamounts in an under-explored region in Costa Rica. The primary=
 target is the Dorado Outcrop, where a =E2=80=9Cgarden=E2=80=9D of female o=
ctopuses was first discovered in 2013 brooding their eggs along low-tempera=
ture vents, a phenomenon scientists had never seen before. The goal for thi=
s expedition is to better understand the hydrogeology, microbiology, ecolog=
y, and geochemistry that may facilitate this fascinating behavior.</p>

<h1 style=3D"font-size: 20px; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; ma=

<p style=3D"margin-bottom: 1.0em; color: #232323; font: 13px/1.5 Arial, Hel=
vetica, sans-serif;">Models represent systems of interrelated ideas, events=
, or processes. The <a href=3D"https://lnks.gd/l/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiJ9.eyJid=
WxsZXRpbl9saW5rX2lkIjoyMTMsInVyaSI6ImJwMjpjbGljayIsInVybCI6Imh0dHBzOi8vd3d3=
LmJpb2ludGVyYWN0aXZlLm9yZy9jbGFzc3Jvb20tcmVzb3VyY2VzL21vZGVsLWJ1aWxkZXI_dXR=
tX21lZGl1bT1lbWFpbCZ1dG1fc291cmNlPUdvdkRlbGl2ZXJ5IiwiYnVsbGV0aW5faWQiOiIyMD=
IzMDYwNi43NzgxMDMyMSJ9.hQrRGauhJ3sF-B-prD1vbuveWBTRsxO7msgJEzvuFt0/s/300660=
7045/br/204281882781-l" style=3D"color: #1D5782;"><em>Model Builder</em></a=
> allows students to generate and refine a variety of models to show relati=
onships and make predictions about biological phenomena. Use a model from t=
he collection developed by <a href=3D"https://lnks.gd/l/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiJ=
9.eyJidWxsZXRpbl9saW5rX2lkIjoyMTQsInVyaSI6ImJwMjpjbGljayIsInVybCI6Imh0dHBzO=
i8vd3d3LmJpb2ludGVyYWN0aXZlLm9yZy8_dXRtX21lZGl1bT1lbWFpbCZ1dG1fc291cmNlPUdv=
dkRlbGl2ZXJ5IiwiYnVsbGV0aW5faWQiOiIyMDIzMDYwNi43NzgxMDMyMSJ9.OOvK2Buclhdm3D=
PfxaW_ugOwxGAjPN5HlDjuYhDXvDM/s/3006607045/br/204281882781-l" style=3D"colo=
r: #1D5782;">BioInteractive</a>, or have students generate their own models=
 with provided graphics. The tool also includes an automated self-check fea=
ture for students and allows educators to score students=E2=80=99 models au=
tomatically.</p>

<h1 style=3D"font-size: 20px; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; ma=
rgin: 0 0 5px; padding: 0;"><strong>Investing in Our Ocean Future:&nbsp; ST=
EM Education Grants to Broaden Access to Ocean Sciences </strong></h1>
<h3 style=3D"font-size: 15px; font-family: Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif; ma=
rgin: 3px 0 4px; padding: 0;"><strong>Proposals Accepted: June 15 - August =
15, 2023 </strong></h3>
<p style=3D"margin-bottom: 1.0em; color: #232323; font: 13px/1.5 Arial, Hel=
vetica, sans-serif;">The National Marine Sanctuary Foundation, in cooperati=
on with NOAA Ocean Exploration, is excited to once again offer grants to ed=
ucators and education programs leading workforce development initiatives th=
at advance diversity, equity, inclusion, and accessibility in ocean science=
 and/or exploration career pathways. The overarching goal is to support a f=
uture ocean workforce that is more representative of US demographics by fun=
ding projects that minimize barriers to entry and retention of diverse yout=
h from communities historically marginalized from ocean science and explora=
tion industries. These grants are an investment in projects and partners th=
at are leading science, education, technology, and engineering (STEM) educa=
tion programming for diverse youth in middle school, high school, undergrad=
uate, and/or community college to learn about the ocean, develop or advance=
 STEM skills, and increase awareness of ocean science careers.</p>
<p style=3D"margin-bottom: 1.0em; color: #232323; font: 13px/1.5 Arial, Hel=
vetica, sans-serif;"><a href=3D"https://lnks.gd/l/eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiJ9.eyJi=
dWxsZXRpbl9saW5rX2lkIjoyMTcsInVyaSI6ImJwMjpjbGljayIsInVybCI6Imh0dHBzOi8vb2N=

RpdW09ZW1haWwmdXRtX3NvdXJjZT1Hb3ZEZWxpdmVyeSIsImJ1bGxldGluX2lkIjoiMjAyMzA2M=
DYuNzc4MTAzMjEifQ.RmmnHy4jG0QKk6gcstET1L55wUhALGApOfulE6fYgy8/s/3006607045/=
br/204281882781-l" style=3D"color: #1D5782;">Learn more about the grants an=
d explore previously funded projects!</a><u></u></p>
